## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard setting of chemical kinetics where reaction mechanisms are modeled by rate laws (often autonomous in A, sometimes explicitly time-dependent via forcing, changing conditions, or deactivation). With only (t, A) available, plausible models are single-species decay/relaxation, nonlinear (reaction-order) kinetics, or time-varying effective rate constants.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zeroth-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption when surface/photochemical limitation dominates)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; leads to exponential A(t))
- Pseudo-first-order with source term: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 (net production minus first-order loss; approach to steady state)
- Relaxation to equilibrium setpoint: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (linear return toward A_eq = c1)
- nth-order (power-law) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general reaction order; c1 can be non-integer)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type consumption with carrying capacity: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating then self-limiting dynamics)
- Inhibited/limited rate (rational): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (effective rate saturates at high A due to inhibition/transport limits)
- General rational kinetics: dA_dt = -(c0 * A + c1 * A**2) / (1 + c2 * A) (combines multiple orders with saturation/feedback)
- Stretched-exponential time-varying rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (effective k(t) changes exponentially with time, e.g., temperature ramp or activation)
- Polynomial-in-time rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * t + c2 * t**2) * A (slow drift in conditions or catalyst activity)
- Catalyst deactivation on rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (rate slows down as active sites deactivate over time)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., chopped light/oscillatory feed): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (time-periodic modulation of effective kinetics)
- Bimolecular loss approximated as single-species: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (self-reaction or A + A â†’ products in a closed approximation)
- Mixed-order loss: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel first- and second-order pathways)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action kinetics often implies dA_dt is proportional to A**n (reaction order), giving power-law dependence on concentration.
- Consumption-only mechanisms typically enforce dA_dt <= 0 for A >= 0, so models often include an overall negative sign multiplying nonnegative functions of A and t.
- Approach-to-equilibrium behavior is captured by linear (c1 - A) factors, producing exponential relaxation toward a steady concentration.
- Multiple parallel pathways appear as sums of terms with different powers of A (e.g., A and A**2), representing competing mechanisms.
- Transport limitation or inhibition commonly yields rational forms where the effective rate flattens at large A (numerator grows ~A^m while denominator grows ~A).
- Changing experimental conditions (temperature ramps, illumination schedules, feed changes) introduce explicit time dependence through k(t) factors multiplying A or A**n.
- Catalyst activation/deactivation is often modeled by exponentially decaying (or increasing) prefactors in time multiplying the concentration-dependent rate.
- Physical concentrations require positivity; structurally, rate laws are often built so that A = 0 is an invariant point (terms include a factor A so dA_dt = 0 at A = 0).
